## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the rate law dA/dt = f(A, t) for a chemical reaction. The rate of concentration change is most commonly a function of the current concentration A through power-law, rational, or exponential forms, with possible explicit time dependence for non-autonomous or forced systems.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- General n-th order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (fractional or integer order kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with reverse reaction or equilibrium offset)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (autocatalytic reaction network)
- Logistic-type rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * A) (self-limiting reaction with product inhibition)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate coefficient)
- Power-law with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (dispersive kinetics in heterogeneous media)
- Rational form two-term: dA_dt = (c0 * A + c1 * A**2) / (1 + c2 * A) (Langmuir-Hinshelwood type)
- Exponential concentration dependence: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * A) (activated or cooperative kinetics)
- Square root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (dissociative adsorption or half-order reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A^n with n close to an integer, it likely reflects the molecularity of an elementary reaction step
- A constant offset in the rate expression (dA_dt = c0*A + c1) suggests a reversible reaction approaching equilibrium or a constant source/sink term
- Rational forms like A/(c+A) indicate surface-catalyzed or enzyme-mediated reactions with saturation at high concentration
- Products of A with polynomial corrections in A (e.g., A*(1-c*A)) suggest autocatalytic or self-inhibiting mechanisms
- Explicit time dependence in the rate law (beyond through A(t)) indicates non-autonomous conditions such as varying temperature, light intensity, or catalyst deactivation
- Fractional power-law exponents (e.g., A^0.5) often arise from quasi-steady-state approximations of multi-step mechanisms
- If the rate changes sign at a particular concentration, a reversible or equilibrium process is indicated, modeled as dA_dt = c0*(A - c1)
- Sigmoidal dependence on A (e.g., A^n/(c+A^n) with n>1) indicates cooperative or allosteric binding kinetics
